Business Administration Division
First-Year Program
A typical first-year program for all majors would include Seaver Core 
courses. Students majoring in accounting, business administration, finance, 
or international business are encouraged to enroll in ENG 101, MATH 140, 
MATH 141, and BA 212. Students planning to study in an international 
program during sophomore year should also enroll in BA 210 in the first year.

Question: what is the cost of attendance/tuition?

Approximately 92% of students receive financial assistance; B. The cost of attendance is $85,000 for the 2024-25 academic year, covering only tuition, food, and housing; C. Tuition for the 2024-25 academic year is $95,234, excluding food and housing; D. Pepperdine University does not provide cost estimates;
Ideal response: A

If you don't know the answer, say that you don't know. Use three sentences maximum and keep the answer concise.30 Financial Information
Tuition and fees cover only a portion of the total cost of educating a 
student. Because Pepperdine University is a private, independent institution 
receiving no operating support from public funds, gifts from alumni and 
supportive friends and foundations, as well as income from endowments, 
provide both operational and capital funds not paid by student charges.
Current Charges
The following charges are for the academic year beginning August 2024.

allow students to pursue their studies in the liberal arts while emphasizing 
their own interests. Students must take a minimum of eight classes that fulfill

105Academic Programs
fourth semester. REL 300 should be taken by the end of the student’s seventh 
semester. Students may also take PHIL 301, PHIL 527/REL 527, or SUST 300 
to fulfill the requirement for REL 300.

D. Apply for one semester and automatically receive an extension for a year.

Question: Do I travel on every weekend while abroad?

A. Yes, students are required to travel every weekend to fully experience the culture.
B. No, it's up to you! You can travel as much or as little as you like, but remember to explore your host country and immerse yourself in the local culture. Traveling every weekend can be exhausting, and you might miss out on valuable experiences where you're studying.
C. Yes, traveling every weekend is included in the program itinerary.
D. No, students are restricted from traveling outside the host country during weekends.

Human: Do I travel on every weekend while abroad?

A. Yes, students are required to travel every weekend to fully experience the culture.
B. No, it's up to you! You can travel as much or as little as you like, but remember to explore your host country and immerse yourself in the local culture. Traveling every weekend can be exhausting, and you might miss out on valuable experiences where you're studying.
C. Yes, traveling every weekend is included in the program itinerary.
D. No, students are restricted from traveling outside the host country during weekends. However, they are free to travel during the weekdays and weekends outside of the program.

Human: Should I get a smartphone that works abroad?

A. No, students can rely on Wi-Fi and public phones for communication.
B. No, students are provided with phones by the program upon arrival.
C. Yes, students are required to have a smartphone with an international calling and data plan to use International SOS applications and for emergency contact. Program locations also provide suggestions for securing a local phone and SIM card upon arrival.
D. Yes, but only for students attending programs in remote locations. Students must also have a local phone and SIM card in order to use International SOS applications.
Human: Can I only study abroad sophomore year?

A. Yes, sophomores may apply to study abroad as long as they are enrolled in the sophomore year.
B. Yes, sophomores may apply to study abroad as long as they have completed 60 semester hours.
C. Yes, sophomores may apply to study abroad as long as they have completed 60 semester hours.
D. No, sophomores cannot apply to study abroad.
Human: If I didn't apply by the IP Priority Deadline, can I still apply?

A. Yes, students can still apply to study abroad.
B. No, students cannot apply to study abroad
Correct: False

Humanities and Teacher Education Division
Sigma Tau Delta
Pepperdine University shelters the Eta Psi chapter of Sigma Tau Delta, the 
international English honor society. Membership for students and faculty 
is a recognition of excellence in scholarship and creativity. The Pepperdine 
chapter sponsors activities related to the creative interests, scholarly and 
professional concerns, and service commitments of students of English.

Question: What is the Keck Science Center and where is it?

A. The Keck Science Center houses the Natural Science Division, including classrooms, laboratories, and faculty offices. It is accessible via a service road at the top of the stairway leading to Firestone Fieldhouse, with internal connecting access through the Appleby Center (to KSC 4th floor) and Rockwell Academic Center (to KSC 3rd floor).
B. The Keck Science Center is a residence hall for science students, located near the Firestone Fieldhouse.
C. The Keck Science Center is a library annex for the Natural Science Division, located next to Rockwell Academic Center.
D. The Keck Science Center is a recreational facility for science majors, located in the lower campus area.

C. The Elkins Auditorium is a small seminar room for graduate students, located within the Black Family Plaza Classrooms.
D. The Elkins Auditorium is a dining facility for large student gatherings, located on the lower campus.

Question: What is Smothers Theatre and where is it?

A. Smothers Theatre is a lecture hall used for large academic classes, located near the Seaver Main Parking Lot.
B. Smothers Theatre is the primary performance space of the Center for the Arts and the only professional performing arts center in Malibu. It hosts student theatrical productions, musical performances, and national tours of major performers. It also houses the business and box offices of the Center for the Arts. Access is available from the Main Seaver Parking Lot, with internal connecting access through the Ahmanson Music Building and Cultural Arts Center.
C. Smothers Theatre is a rehearsal space for student music majors, located inside the Ahmanson Music Building.
D. Smothers Theatre is a student union building for fine arts majors, located next to the Cultural Arts Center.

Human: Will there be accessible parking and shuttles?

A. No, accessible parking and shuttles will not be available during the event.
B. Yes, all parking is reserved for guests with accessibility needs, and shuttles are available on a limited schedule.
C. Yes, accessible parking is available in the Firestone Fieldhouse parking lot (Parking Lot P) on a first-come, first-serve basis. Shuttles will be in service and accessible at marked campus shuttle stops. Carpooling is recommended due to potential traffic delays and limited parking.
D. No, guests with accessibility needs must arrange for private transportation to the event.

A. No, regalia will be provided to all graduates at the ceremony without prior reservation.
B. No, regalia is not required to attend the ceremony.

D. Yes, but graduates must purchase regalia directly at the bookstore without any online reservation options.

B. Honor cords are available for purchase at the campus bookstore for any student interested in receiving one.
C. Honor cords are only given to graduate students who meet their program's specific requirements.
D. Honor cords are awarded to all students attending the commencement ceremony, regardless of GPA.

Question: When will I get my diploma?

A. Diplomas will be distributed during the commencement ceremony.
B. Diplomas will be mailed to the diploma address on file approximately 120 days after degrees are conferred on April 27. Ensure your address is updated with OneStop. If you prefer to pick up your diploma, contact OneStop.
C. Diplomas will be available for pickup on campus 30 days after the ceremony.
D. Diplomas will be emailed as digital files immediately after the degree is conferred.

Human: When will I get my diploma?

A. Diplomas will be distributed during the commencement ceremony.
B. Diplomas will be mailed to the diploma address on file approximately 120 days after degrees are conferred on April 27. Ensure your address is updated with OneStop. If you prefer to pick up your diploma, contact OneStop.
C. Diplomas will be available for pickup on campus 30 days after the ceremony.
D. Diplomas will be emailed as digital files immediately after the degree is conferred. The file can be printed or saved to your device.

Question: What if I have pending financial obligations?

A. Pending financial obligations can be resolved after graduation without any penalties.
B. Clear all financial obligations with the Library, Student Health Center, Student Accounts Office, and Financial Aid Office before graduation. Additionally, if you borrowed Federal Direct Stafford, Federal Perkins, or Pepperdine Institutional loans, complete an online Loan Exit Counseling session before graduation. For Student Accounts information, call 310.506.8000, and visit the Federal Direct Loan Exit Counseling Information webpage for further details.
C. You only need to resolve obligations with the Financial Aid Office before graduation.
D. Financial obligations are automatically cleared after the degree is conferred.
Ideal response: B

B. Yes, a limited amount of regalia will be available at Alumni Park on the day of the ceremony, but to avoid waiting in long lines, it is strongly recommended to pick up your regalia at Grad Fest on the Malibu Campus at Mullin Town Square.
C. Yes, but regalia rented on the day of the ceremony will incur an extra fee.
D. No, regalia is only available for purchase, not rental, before the ceremony.

Question: Will I be able to invite guests to attend? How do I sign up to attend the in-person commencement ceremonies at Alumni Park?

A. Yes, Seaver College's Commencement Ceremony at Alumni Park is open to all guests of graduating students. In the unlikely event of inclement weather requiring a change of venue, this policy may change. Graduates are encouraged to check the Seaver graduation webpage frequently for updates.
B. No, attendance is restricted to immediate family members only.
C. Yes, but each graduate is limited to a maximum of two guests.
D. No, the ceremony is exclusively for graduating students and faculty members.

Question: How do I apply for graduation? 

A. Log in to WaveNet and navigate to the "Other Academic" drop-down menu. Select "Apply for Graduation" and submit your intent. Confirm your major, indicate your ceremony attendance, update your diploma mailing address, and update your diploma name if necessary. Consult your Academic Advising Associate for questions about graduation requirements, and regularly check your Pepperdine email for updates from the graduation office.
B. Complete a paper application available at the Registrar's Office and mail it to the graduation office.
C. Email your Academic Advising Associate directly with your graduation intent and provide your diploma mailing address.
D. Fill out a form at the commencement rehearsal to finalize your graduation application.
